{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-07-30 19:50:09","updatedTime":"2020-07-30 11:50:09","title":"California Road Trip: A 21-Day Suggested Itinerary","link":"https://www.nomadicmatt.com/?p=206817","description":"<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/calithreeweekd.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"An open road in Joshua Tree National Park, California, USA\"><br />\n<strong>Posted</strong>: 7/2/2020 | July 2nd, 2020</p>\n<p>California. It’s the third-largest state in the country and home to over 40 million people and a range of environments and landscapes: dense forests in the north, rugged mountains in the east, majestic deserts in the south, world-class beaches on the coast, and the fabulous wine regions on the coast and central valley. </p>\n<p>And it&#8217;s perfect for road trips. </p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.nomadicmatt.com/travel-blogs/california-road-trip-one-week-itinerary/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\">I’ve already outlined an awesome seven-day itinerary for Southern California</a>, but today I wanted to share a longer, more comprehensive route for anyone who has a few weeks to explore more of the state’s cities and landscapes.</p>\n<p>Even with three weeks, you’ll still miss a lot of great spots in this state (I mean you could spend months traveling California) but this suggested itinerary hits some of my favorite major — and not so major — places.<br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>Days 1–3: San Francisco </h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/calithreeweek2.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The famous Golden Gate Bridge in San Francisco, California\"><br />\n<a href=\"https://www.nomadicmatt.com/travel-guides/united-states-travel-guide/san-francisco/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">San Francisco</a> is one of the most recognizable cities in the US. Home to hippies, yuppies, techies, students, and a sizeable immigrant community, it’s a vibrant and diverse city. It is an eclectic destination to visit. Here’s a list of a few of my favorite things to see and do:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><strong>Walk the Golden Gate Bridge</strong> – When it opened, it was the world’s longest and tallest suspension bridge, stretching some 4,200 feet. It offers incredible views of the bay and the ships coming and going. You can walk across it too. </li>\n<li><strong>Tour Alcatraz</strong> – Alcatraz is one of the most infamous former prisons in the country. It housed some of the nation’s worst criminals, such as Al Capone. Today, it’s a national landmark where you can take tours of the prison, step foot in the cells, and learn about its history.</li>\n<li><strong>Visit the Beat Museum</strong> – Dedicated to the 1950s Beat Generation, this unique museum houses original manuscripts, rare books, letters, and more from authors like Jack Kerouac and Allen Ginsberg. It also holds regular events, so check the website to see if anything is happening during your visit.</li>\n<li><strong>Take a food tour</strong> – San Francisco is known for its foodie culture. If you want to cast a wide culinary net and try a lot of different cuisines and dishes, consider taking a food tour. Some companies to check out are <a href=\"https://wildsftours.com/tour/food-crawl/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Wild SF Tours</a>, <a href=\"https://www.secretfoodtours.com/san-francisco/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Secret Food Tours</a>, and <a href=\"https://tastebudtours.com/food-tours/san-francisco-food-tour-a-taste-of-little-italy/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">TasteBud Tours</a>.</li>\n<li><strong>Explore Chinatown</strong> – When immigrants from China first came to America, many set up shop in San Francisco. Today, in the biggest Chinatown in the U.S., you’ll find some of the best Chinese food in the country, as well as wonderful teahouses, bars, souvenir stalls, and fortune cookie makers.</li>\n<li><strong>Relax at Golden Gate Park</strong> – This gigantic park a great place to walk or relax. It features a Japanese garden, museums, an arboretum, a carousel, and many hiking and walking trails. It’s 20% bigger than New York’s Central Park so you easily could spend an entire day here!</li>\n</ul>\n<p>For more suggestions, <a href=\"https://www.nomadicmatt.com/travel-blogs/things-to-see-and-do-in-san-francisco/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">here’s a detailed list of things to see and do in San Francisco</a>.</p>\n<p><strong>Where to Stay</strong></p>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fpwa%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FHI-San-Francisco-Downtown%2FSan-Francisco%2F4549\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">HI San Francisco – Downtown</a> – HI Downtown has some standard perks, like free breakfast and free towels, but the staff also organize a lot of events, including pub crawls, trips to Muir Woods and Yosemite, and bike tours across the Golden Gate Bridge. </li>\n<li><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FGreen-Tortoise-Hostel%2FSan-Francisco%2F1821\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Green Tortoise Hostel</a> – This lively hostel is my favorite in the city. It offers free breakfast, free dinners multiple times per week, and even a free sauna! It’s a party hostel, so be sure to stay here only if you’re looking to meet people and get rowdy.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>For more suggestions, <a href=\"https://www.nomadicmatt.com/travel-blogs/best-hostels-in-san-francisco/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">here’s a full list of my favorite hostels in San Francisco!</a><br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>Day 4: Big Sur</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/calithreeweek3.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The rugged coasts and blue waters of Big Sur, California\"><br />\nOn the coast just over two hours south of San Francisco is a 90-mile expanse of stunning views and massive redwoods known as Big Sur. There are plenty of beautiful beaches, hiking trails, viewpoints, and campgrounds in case you want to stay overnight (which I recommend). It’s one of the most beautiful stretches of craggy, unspoiled coastline in the state, so take your time exploring as you head south.</p>\n<p><strong>Where to Stay</strong><br />\nI suggest staying at least one night around Big Sur (or just south of the region) to split up the drive to LA. If you don’t have camping gear, <a href=\"http://airbnb.7eer.net/c/214481/264339/4273\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Airbnb</a> has a lot of places around the area. You can also just pop into any of numerous cheap motels in the area too.<br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>Days 5–7: Los Angeles</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/calithreeweek4.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The picuresque Santa Monica beach and ferris wheel\"><br />\nThough I hated it when I first visited, <a href=\"https://www.nomadicmatt.com/travel-blogs/loving-los-angeles/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">I’ve come to love Los Angeles</a>. It’s not a “tourist” city: everything is spread out and there are not many attractions as you’d expect. But, if you come to LA and go with the flow like a local, you’ll see why people love it so much. This is a city where you eat, drink, hike the many trails in the area, and linger in a coffeeshop. </p>\n<p>Here are some suggestions on how to fill your days:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><strong>Hit the beach</strong> – Venice Beach is an iconic LA hotspot where you’ll encounter all kinds of street performers, surfers, rollerskaters, and both locals and tourists alike soaking up the sun. Other beaches worth checking out are Carbon Beach, Santa Monica State Beach, Huntington City Beach, and El Matador.\n<li><strong>See the Le Brea Tar Pits</strong> – Located in Hancock Park, these natural asphalt pits have existed for over 50,000 years. Tons of fossils preserved for centuries have been found in the pits, and there’s a museum nearby that has lots of interesting information about them and how they came to be.\n<li><strong>See the Hollywood Sign</strong> – You can snap pictures of the sign from pretty much anywhere in Hollywood. However, it’s also possible to hike up to the sign itself to take in the view. The three trails that you can take (from easiest to hardest) are the Mt. Hollywood Trail, the Brush Canyon Trail, and the Cahuenga Peak Trail. Bring water, because the hike will take a few hours.</li>\n<li><strong>Visit LACMA</strong> &#8211;  Home to some 150,000 works, the LA County Museum of Art is the largest art museum in the western USA. They have collections from pretty much every era throughout history and every region of the world. Admission is $25 USD.</li>\n<li><strong>Visit The Last Bookstore</strong> &#8211; This is one of my favorite bookstores in the world. It also sells records, has art displays, and features a cool upstairs area with cheap used books. Browse the shelves, grab a coffee, and buy a book for your journey.</li>\n<li><strong>Stroll down Hollywood Boulevard</strong> – Don’t miss the Walk of Fame (where celebrities have their names engraved in the sidewalk) and Grauman’s Chinese Theatre (featuring celebrities’ handprints and footprints). </li>\n<li><strong>Visit the Getty Museum</strong> – This art museum opened in 1997 and boasts a diverse collection paintings, manuscripts, drawings, and other artwork. The collection runs from the eighth century to the present day, so there is something for everyone. Admission is free.</li>\n<li><strong>Go hiking</strong> – Get out and stretch your legs on the city’s hiking trails. Some worth checking out are the Charlie Turner Trail (90 minutes), Baldwin Hills (30 minutes), Runyon Canyon (45 minutes), Portuguese Bend Reserve (3 hours), and Echo Mountain (3-3.5 hours).</li>\n<li><strong>Visit The Broad</strong> – This contemporary art museum is one of the city’s newest. Opened in 2015, it has over 2,000 pieces of art. It also has a rotating series of temporary exhibitions too (check the website to see what’s on during your visit). Admission is free.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>For a much longer list on what to see and do in LA, <a href=\"https://www.nomadicmatt.com/travel-guides/united-states-travel-guide/los-angeles/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">check out my Los Angeles travel guide</a>.</p>\n<p>Moreover, the city also has innumerable world-class food options. Some places I really like are Musso &#038; Frank Grill, Dan Tana’s, Meals by Genet, The Butcher’s Daughter, Sugarfish, and Thai Pepper. </p>\n<p><strong>Where to Stay</strong></p>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FBanana-Bungalow-Hollywood%2FLos-Angeles%2F11182\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Banana Bungalow Hollywood</a> – A laid-back but social hostel that organizes lots of activities and makes it easy to meet people. If you want to party and have fun, this is the place for you!</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FFreehand-Los-Angeles%2FLos-Angeles%2F272919\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Freehand Los Angeles</a> – This hostel/hotel features designer rooms with comfortable beds, a rooftop pool and bar with amazing views of the city, a lobby bar, a restaurant, and even a fitness center. </li>\n</ul>\n<p>For more suggestions, <a href=\"https://www.nomadicmatt.com/travel-blogs/best-hostels-in-los-angeles/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">here’s a list of my favorite hostels in Los Angeles.</a><br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>Days 8–9: San Diego</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/calithreeweek5.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The wide, white-sand Pacific Beach near San Diego, California\"><br />\nSan Diego, just two hours down the coast, has just as much to offer. It’s easier to navigate (it’s smaller), the weather is always perfect, the beaches are better, and it’s cheaper too. After LA, it’s my favorite city in the state. Spend a day or two soaking up the city. </p>\n<p>Here are some suggestions for things to see and do during your visit:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><strong>Visit the USS Midway Museum</strong> – This aircraft carrier, commissioned right after World War II, was the largest ship in the world until 1955 and saw action in numerous conflicts, including Vietnam. It was decommissioned in 1992 and became a museum. You can explore the flight deck as well as many of the rooms below. </li>\n<li><strong>Hike Point Loma</strong> – This is the peninsula where Europeans first arrived in California. Walk out to the tip and enjoy the serene views, visit the lighthouse (built in 1855), and watch locals climb the rocks and cliffs of Osprey Point.</li>\n<li><strong>Visit the San Diego Zoo</strong> – This is one of the best zoos in the country. Located in Balboa Park (see below), it has over 3,500 animals and 700,000 plant species. It’s a massive, 1,800-acre park where you could easily spend an entire day. If you’re traveling with kids, don’t miss it. </li>\n<li><strong>Explore Balboa Park</strong> – In addition to the zoo, Balboa Park also offers dozens of museums as well as walking paths, sports fields, gardens, greenhouses, stadiums, theatres, and much more. It’s one of the oldest recreational parks in the country.</li>\n<li><strong>Enjoy Pacific Beach</strong> – If you want to soak up the sun, swim, or surf, head to Pacific Beach. If you’re a night owl, the area also has lots of bars, clubs, and restaurants too.</li>\n<li><strong>Go whale watching</strong> – California gray whales, which can grow up to 49 feet and live for over 70 years, migrate from Alaska to Mexico each year between December and April. They are incredible to see up close, and tours are quite affordable (usually around $35 USD).</li>\n<li><strong>Relax in Belmont Park</strong> – This is a kitschy amusement park right next to the ocean. It has a few classic rides, as well as games and lots of greasy (and delicious) snacks. It’s cheesy but fun!</li>\n<li><strong>Go surfing</strong> – Whether you’re a veteran or a newbie, grab a board and hit the waves. There’s some awesome surfing here. You can usually rent a board for around $30 USD a day. Lessons cost around $70 USD and last 90-minutes. </li>\n</ul>\n<p><strong>Where to Stay</strong></p>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FHI-San-Diego-Downtown%2FSan-Diego%2F1856\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">HI San Diego</a> – HI San Diego organizes lots of events and tours that make it easy to meet other travelers. They include free breakfast and also have a big kitchen so you can cook your own food to save money. </li>\n<li><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FITH-Adventure-Hostel-San-Diego%2FSan-Diego%2F66491%3FdateFrom%3D2020-08-26%26dateTo%3D2020-08-27%26number_of_guests%3D1\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">ITH Adventure Hostel</a> – This is an eco-friendly hostel with a vegetable garden (guests get free veggies), a recycling and compost program, and even backyard chickens. There is lots of outdoor common space to relax in too. </li>\n</ul>\n<p>If you’re on a budget, <a href=\"https://www.nomadicmatt.com/travel-blogs/best-hostels-san-diego/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">here’s a list of the best hostels in San Diego for you.</a><br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>Days 10–12: Joshua Tree National Park</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/calithreeweek6.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The beautiful and unique Joshua trees in Joshua Tree National Park, California\"><br />\nLocated just under three hours from San Diego and sandwiched between the Mojave and Colorado Deserts, this is where you’ll find the iconic Joshua trees (Yucca brevifolia), twisted multibranched trees. Towering boulders dot the arid landscape and swaths of cacti poke up from the hard dirt. It’s an otherworldly place perfect for hiking, camping, and escaping the busy cities along California’s coast.</p>\n<p>The park was declared a national monument in 1936 and designated a national park in 1994. There are a lot of trails here, so consult the trail map when you visit. Some of my favorites are:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><strong>Barker Dam Trail</strong> – A quick 1.1-mile loop on which you can see wildlife such as rabbits, bighorn sheep, and all kinds of birds.</li>\n<li><strong>Wall Street Mill</strong> – An easy 2.8-mile hike that leads to an old mill used to refine ore from nearby gold mines.</li>\n<li><strong>Ryan Mountain</strong> &#8211; A steep 3-mile hike offering some incredible views.</li>\n<li><strong>Split Rock Loop</strong> – A quiet 2-mile hike with lots of neat rock formations.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>A seven-day vehicle pass for the park is $30 USD (it allows multiple entries in case you stay in one of the nearby towns).</p>\n<p><strong>Where to Stay</strong><br />\n<a href=\"http://airbnb.7eer.net/c/214481/264339/4273\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Airbnb</a> is the best option if you don’t have your own camping gear, although there are also glamping and more rustic options.<br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>Days 13–15: Sequoia National Park &#038; Kings Canyon National Park</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/calithreeweek7.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The massive redwoods and sequoias in Sequoia National Park, California\"><br />\nSequoia National Park, established in 1890, is where you’ll find the largest single-stem tree in the entire world. Named “General Sherman,” this giant sequoia tree stands a whopping 275 feet tall and has a diameter of 25 feet (that’s a 103-foot circumference). It’s so big that one of its branches is bigger than almost every single tree east of the Mississippi.</p>\n<p>Start your visit at the Giant Forest Museum to learn about the history, geography, and importance of the park and its flora and fauna. Afterward, walk the Big Trees Trail, a short loop that will get you in and amongst the trees so you can see them up close. </p>\n<p>For a sweeping view of the forest and surrounding landscape, hike up Moro Rock, a massive 250-foot granite dome that juts out of the surrounding hills and forest. Stairs and a concrete viewpoint were built into the rock itself, so you can safely climb to the top and enjoy the magnificent vista.</p>\n<p>And for more hiking options and beautiful scenery, visit nearby Kings Canyon National Park. Here you’ll find “General Grant” (the third largest tree in the world). For a scenic drive, cruise along the Kings Canyon Scenic Byway. </p>\n<p>Both parks are around 4-6 hours from Joshua Tree.</p>\n<p><strong>Where to Stay</strong><br />\nThere are tons of places to camp here (both inside and outside of the parks). However, there are also lots of lodges and hotels if camping is not for you. <a href=\"http://www.booking.com/index.html?aid=362916\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Booking.com</a> has the best list of them all.<br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>Days 16–18: Yosemite National Park</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/calithreeweek8.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The beautiful scenery of Yosemite National Park, California\"><br />\nLocated in the Sierra Nevada mountain range two hours from Sequoia National Park and encompassing nearly 750,000 acres, Yosemite is one of the most iconic national parks in the country. It’s where you’ll find El Capitán, the towering granite cliff you’ve likely seen on social media (it was also featured in the movie, <em>Free Solo</em>). It is one of the most popular parks in the US, seeing over four million visitors each year who enjoy hiking, biking, climbing, camping, rafting, canoeing, and kayaking here. </p>\n<p>Here are a few hiking suggestions to help you get started:</p>\n<ul>\n<li><strong>Mirror Lake</strong> – An easy 2-mile hike to Mirror Lake. Takes 1-2 hours.</li>\n<li><strong>Nevada Fall Trail</strong> – A challenging 5.8-mile hike to the top of the Nevada Falls waterfall. Takes 5–6 hours.</li>\n<li><strong>Tuolumne Grove Nature Trail</strong> – An easy 2.5-mile hike around a grove filled with massive giant sequoia trees. Takes 1–2 hours.</li>\n<li><strong>Elizabeth Lake Trail</strong> – A moderate 4.8-mile hike that leads to Elizabeth Lake, a glacier-carved lake at the base of Unicorn Peak. Takes 4–5 hours.</li>\n<li><strong>Eagle Peak Trail</strong> – A difficult 6.9-mile hike to the top of Eagle Peak and back. Takes 8 hours.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Be sure to visit the visitor’s center on arrival to get information on activities, prices, and information on the latest weather.</p>\n<p><strong>Where to Stay</strong><br />\nIf you aren’t planning to camp, there are actually many other options here. Lodges, resorts, and hotels can be found both inside the park and all around it. Use <a href=\"http://airbnb.7eer.net/c/214481/264339/4273\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Airbnb</a> or <a href=\"http://www.booking.com/index.html?aid=362916\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Booking.com</a> to find a place to stay.<br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>Days 19–20: Napa Valley</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/calithreeweek9.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"A hot air balloon floating over vineyards in Napa Valley, California\"><br />\nFinally, head northwest to Napa Valley, one of the world’s premier wine regions, and end your trip relaxing at a vineyard. Napa is just over three hours from Yosemite and offers a plethora of world-class wine and food to indulge in.</p>\n<p>While it’s a particularly expensive region of the state, it is possible to <a href=\"https://www.nomadicmatt.com/travel-blogs/napa-valley-on-a-budget/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">visit Napa Valley on a budget</a> if you plan ahead and share costs with other people. </p>\n<p>If you’re on a budget, stick to the markets and sandwich shops. Gott’s Roadside has locations in both Napa and St. Helena and serves delicious burgers for under $10 USD, while Ad Hoc runs a delicious food truck offering fried chicken made by a Michelin-star chef for $15 USD with sides. </p>\n<p><strong>Whereto Stay</strong><br />\nWhile some vineyards offer accommodation, they are usually super expensive. Unless you’re looking to splurge, use <a href=\"http://airbnb.7eer.net/c/214481/264339/4273\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Airbnb</a>. I find the best value accommodation in the area on that site.<br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>Day 21: Back to San Francisco</h3>\n<p>It’s time to head back to San Francisco. The drive is around 90 minutes, so you’ll have plenty of time to make stops along the way if you see anything that piques your interest.</p>\n<p><center>***</center></p>\n<p>This three-week itinerary will help you cover a lot of ground without being too rushed. Adjust the route as you go (or based on the amount of time you have). But, no matter the route you pick, the diversity and beauty of California will ensure you&#8217;ll have a wonderful road trip.  </p>\n<div class=\"single-booking\">\n<h4>Book Your Trip to the USA: Logistical Tips and Tricks</h4>\n<p><strong>Book Your Flight</strong><br />\nFind a cheap flight by using <a href=\"http://www.anrdoezrs.net/click-3032045-12837948\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Skyscanner</a> or <a href=\"https://www.momondo.com/\">Momondo</a>. They are my two favorite search engines because they search websites and airlines around the globe so you always know no stone is left unturned.</p>\n<p><strong>Book Your Accommodation</strong><br />\nYou can book your hostel with <a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Hostelworld</a>. If you want to stay elsewhere, use <a href=\"https://www.booking.com/index.html?aid=362916\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Booking.com</a> as they consistently return the cheapest rates for guesthouses and cheap hotels. </p>\n<p><strong>Don&#8217;t Forget Travel Insurance</strong><br />\nTravel insurance will protect you against illness, injury, theft, and cancellations. />\n<strong>Posted</strong>: 7/27/20 | July 27th, 2020</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.nomadicmatt.com/travel-guides/costa-rica-travel-tips/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Costa Rica</a> was the very first place I ever visited, kick-staring a journey that would eventually take me around the world and launch my career as a travel writer. Since that first trip, I&#8217;ve returned a few times, lured in by the friendly people, cloud forests, wildlife, and excellent beaches. </p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.nomadicmatt.com/travel-guides/costa-rica-travel-tips/san-jose/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">San José</a> is the starting point for most visitors in the country, owing to the fact that it&#8217;s the nation&#8217;s capital and a major international hub. Chances are you&#8217;ll be here for a few days as you get situated before heading off to hike, lounge on the beach, and enjoy the lush and scenic landscapes. </p>\n<p>I&#8217;ve been staying in hostels for over a decade during my several return visits to Costa Rica. There are <a href=\"https://www.nomadicmatt.com/travel-blogs/how-to-pick-a-good-hostel/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">a lot of things to consider when selecting a hostel</a> in San José. The top four are:</p>\n<ol>\n<li><strong>Location</strong> – San José is huge, and it can take some time to get around. Pick a place that is central to the sites and nightlife you want to see. All the hostels listed here are in good locations.</li>\n<li><strong>Price</strong> – In San José, you really get what you pay for, so if you go with a really cheap one, you&#8217;re probably going to get a hostel that is small and cramped and doesn&#8217;t offer great service.</li>\n<li><strong>Amenities</strong> – Every hostel in the city offers free Wi-Fi, and most have a free breakfast, but if you want more than that, be sure to do your research to find the hostel that best meets your needs!</li>\n<li><strong>Staff</strong> – All the hostels listed here have amazing staff! They are super friendly and knowledgeable. Even if you don&#8217;t stay at one of the places listed below, be sure to look up reviews to ensure you end up somewhere where the staff is helpful and friendly. They can make or break a hostel!</li>\n</ol>\n<p>Here is my list of the hostels in San José that I like the most. If you don’t want to read the longer list below, the following hostels are the best in each category:</p>\n<p><strong>Best Hostel for Budget Travelers</strong>: <a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fpwa%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FCosta-Rica-Backpackers%2FSan-Jose%2F870\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">Costa Rica Backpackers</a><br />\n<strong>Best Hostel for Families</strong>: <a Cat Hostel</a><br />\n<strong>Best Hostel for Digital Nomads</strong>: <a Pangea</a> or <a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fpwa%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FCosta-Rica-Backpackers%2FSan-Jose%2F870\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">Costa Rica Backpackers</a><br />\n<strong>Best Overall Hostel</strong>: <a noreferrer\">Capital Hostel de Ciudad</a></p>\n<p>Want the specifics of each hostel? Here&#8217;s my comprehensive list of the best hostels in San José:</p>\n<p><strong>Price Legend (per night)</strong></p>\n<ul>\n<li>$ = Under $10 USD</li>\n<li>$$ = $10-20 USD</li>\n<li>$$$ = Over $20 USD</li>\n</ul>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<h3>1. Capital Hostel de Ciudad</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/sanjosehostel1.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The cozy bunk beds of the Capital Hostel in San José, Costa Rica\"><br />\nThis is a chill hostel with cozy beds and lots of common space. It has a co-living space as well, making it a good choice for anyone working remotely. There&#8217;s a patio for BBQs and yoga, a game room with a pool table and projector for watching movies, and a fully equipped kitchen (breakfast is included). The mattresses are pretty thick and the beds have privacy curtains. Overall, it offers a nice balance of being a relaxed but social hostel.</p>\n<p><strong>Capital Hostel de Ciudad at a glance</strong>:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>$$</li>\n<li>Relaxed atmosphere</li>\n<li>Game room &#038; coworking space</li>\n<li>Outdoor patio for hanging out</li>\n</ul>\n<p><em>Beds from $15 USD a night, rooms from $42 USD.</em></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fpwa%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FCapital-Hostel-de-Ciudad%2FSan-Jose%2F279326\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">—> Book your stay at Capital Hostel de Ciudad!</a><br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>2. Stray Cat Hostel</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/sanjosehostel2.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The colorful interior of the Stray Cat hostel in San José, Costa Rica\"><br />\nThis colorful backpacker hostel is covered in art and murals. It has a cozy, homey vibe while still being well maintained and clean. The mattresses are a little thin (and the bunks don&#8217;t have curtains), but the hostel is quiet and laid back, so it&#8217;s easy to get a decent night&#8217;s sleep. There are female-only dorms too. It&#8217;s close to the bus station as well, making it a convenient location if you&#8217;re just passing through or heading to/from the airport. And, if you&#8217;re an artist, you can trade your skills for free accommodation. </p>\n<p><strong>Stray Cat Hostel at a glance</strong>:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>$$</li>\n<li>Female-only dorms available</li>\n<li>Quiet atmosphere</li>\n<li>Free breakfast</li>\n</ul>\n<p><em>Beds from $12 USD a night, rooms from $40 USD.</em></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fpwa%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FStray-Cat-Hostel%2FSan-Jose%2F285767\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">—> Book your stay at Stray Cat Hostel!</a><br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>3. Costa Rica Backpackers</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/sanjosehostel3.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The fun pool area at Costa Rica Backpackers hostel in San José, Costa Rica\"><br />\nThis is a lively, social hostel popular with the younger backpacker/party crowd. It has a pool and bar on-site, and there are organized tours and activities. Breakfast isn&#8217;t included, but there is free coffee all day. The beds aren&#8217;t the best (the mattresses are thin and the bunks squeak) and the bathrooms are small and could use an update, but it&#8217;s the cheapest hostel in the city. If you&#8217;re on a tight budget and want to party, it&#8217;s the place to be! </p>\n<p><strong>Costa Rica Backpackers at a glance</strong>:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>$</li>\n<li>Pool and bar</li>\n<li>Easy to meet other travelers</li>\n<li>Fun and social atmosphere</li>\n</ul>\n<p><em>Beds from $7 USD a night, rooms from $25 USD.</em></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fpwa%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FCosta-Rica-Backpackers%2FSan-Jose%2F870\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">—> Book your stay at Costa Rica Backpackers!</a><br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>4. Fauna Luxury Hostel</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/sanjosehostel4.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The cozy pod beds at Launa Luxury Hostel in San José, Costa Rica\"><br />\nFauna is a boutique hostel with really cool and cozy pod beds, tons of outdoor common space to lounge, a pool, and lots of really neat artwork in the rooms. The beds have thick mattresses and curtains (two things I really appreciate), breakfast is included, and there is air conditioning (a big plus in Costa Rica!). There are balconies you chill out on that overlook the pool, and the private rooms are super spacious and similar to hotel rooms. They also arrange cheap airport shuttles too. For $8 USD per night, you really get a lot of value here!</p>\n<p><strong>Fauna Luxury Hostel at a glance</strong>:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>$</li>\n<li>Great beds</li>\n<li>Free breakfast</li>\n<li>Laid-back, relaxed vibe</li>\n</ul>\n<p><em>Beds from $8 USD a night, rooms from $39 USD.</em></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fpwa%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FFauna-Luxury-Hostel%2FSan-Jose%2F273530\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">—> Book your stay at Fauna Luxury Hostel!</a><br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>5. Hostel del Paseo</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/sanjosehostel5.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"Games in the common area of Hostel Del Paseo in San José, Costa Rica\"><br />\nThis hostel doesn&#8217;t have a great social vibe, but the dorms are quiet and clean. There is a huge common area with lots of games and movies, and there&#8217;s a bus station nearby. The staff are super helpful, the free breakfast is pretty good, and the dorms are capped at eight beds, so you&#8217;re never crammed in with lots of other people. The beds don&#8217;t have curtains, but the mattresses are thick and comfy, so you&#8217;ll get a decent night&#8217;s sleep.</p>\n<p><strong>Hostel del Paseo at a glance</strong>:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>$$</li>\n<li>Quiet dorms make sleeping easy</li>\n<li>Lots of common rooms &#038; games</li>\n<li>Free breakfast</li>\n</ul>\n<p><em>Beds from $12 USD a night, rooms from $44 USD.</em></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fpwa%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FHostel-Del-Paseo%2FSan-Jose%2F280540\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">—> Book your stay at Hostel del Paseo!</a><br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>6. TripOn Open House</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/sanjosehostel8.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The relaxing patio with hammocks at TripOn Hostel in San José, Costa Rica\"><br />\nThis funky, social hostel is located near supermarkets and tons of restaurants. It has an awesome free breakfast every morning and organizes cheap shuttles to the airport too (which is just 30 minutes away). The beds are comfy and have curtains for privacy and there are lots of common areas for hanging out and socializing. It&#8217;s a really fun hostel, with lots of things to do. There are also hammocks outside for relaxing, video games, and a fully-equipped kitchen if you feel like cooking your own food.</p>\n<p><strong>TripOn Open House at a glance</strong>:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>$$</li>\n<li>Social atmosphere makes it easy to meet people</li>\n<li>Great free breakfast</li>\n<li>Good location</li>\n</ul>\n<p><em>Beds from $10 USD a night, rooms from $43 USD.</em></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fpwa%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FTripOn-Open-House%2FSan-Jose%2F93293\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">—> Book your stay at TripOn Open House!</a><br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>7. In the Wind Hostel &#038; Guesthouse</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/sanjosehostel9a.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The chill common room with colorful couches at In the Wind Hostel in San José, Costa Rica\"><br />\nAnother laid-back hostel, In the Wind has a cool outdoor area for hanging out and having BBQs, offers free breakfast (with pancakes), and has awesome staff. It&#8217;s also super clean, which is always a plus in any hostel. The beds aren&#8217;t amazing (there are no privacy curtains and the mattresses are thin), but the hostel is super affordable and the vibe here more than makes up for it. If you&#8217;re looking for that &#8220;classic&#8221; backpacker hostel experience, you&#8217;ll find it here. </p>\n<p><strong>In the Wind Hostel &#038; Guesthouse at a glance</strong>:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>$$</li>\n<li>Awesome staff</li>\n<li>Free breakfast</li>\n<li>Quiet and calm atmosphere</li>\n</ul>\n<p><em>Beds from $10 USD a night, rooms from $17 USD.</em></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fpwa%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FIn-The-Wind-Hostel-Guesthouse%2FSan-Jose%2F51566\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">—> Book your stay at In the Wind Hostel &#038; Guesthouse!</a><br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>8. Hostel Pangea</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/sanjosehostel10.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The pool and outdoor common area at Hostel Pangea in San José, Costa Rica\"><br />\nThis is a party hostel. It has an on-site bar with super cheap drinks plus a heated pool and a restaurant. There are also daily activities organized by the staff. The dorms are a little small, and the beds are basic metal bunks with no curtains but people come here for the pool and partying. You&#8217;ll find lots of common areas here too so there&#8217;s always a spot to chill out. In short, if you&#8217;re looking to meet lots of people and party, this is where you want to stay. </p>\n<p><strong>Hostel Pangea at a glance</strong>:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>$$</li>\n<li>Bar &#038; pool on-site</li>\n<li>Lots of chill outdoor common areas</li>\n<li>Really cheap drinks</li>\n</ul>\n<p><em>Beds from $10 USD a night, rooms from $30 USD.</em></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fpwa%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FHostel-Pangea%2FSan-Jose%2F3816\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">—> Book your stay at Hostel Pangea!</a></p>\n<p><center>***</center></p>\n<p>With dorms under $10 USD per night and private rooms for under $20 USD, <a href=\"https://www.nomadicmatt.com/travel-guides/costa-rica-travel-tips/san-jose/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">San José</a> is a steal for budget travelers. </p>\n<p>While it&#8217;s not the most exciting destination in <a href=\"https://www.nomadicmatt.com/travel-guides/costa-rica-travel-tips/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Costa Rica</a>, chances are you&#8217;ll be here for a few days before heading off to the country&#8217;s better-known sights. src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/panamahostels.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The towering skyline of Panama City surrounded by its lush green parks\"><br />\n<strong>Posted</strong>: 7/5/20 | July 5th, 2020</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.nomadicmatt.com/travel-guides/panama-travel-tips/panama-city/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Panama City</a> is known as the shipping and financial hub of <a href=\"https://www.nomadicmatt.com/travel-guides/central-america-travel-tips/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Central America</a> — but there&#8217;s much more to it than that.</p>\n<p>Panama City is a bustling, lively city with a vibrant nightlife, tons of history, and delicious food. It&#8217;s a good hub to base yourself in for a few days while you plan your next steps.</p>\n<p>Since it&#8217;s not as cheap as other cities in the region, you&#8217;ll want to save money by booking yourself a hostel while you&#8217;re here. They&#8217;re the most cost-effective (and fun) way to enjoy the city.</p>\n<p>However, there are <a href=\"https://www.nomadicmatt.com/travel-blogs/how-to-pick-a-good-hostel/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">a lot of things to consider when selecting a hostel</a>. The top four in Panama City are:</p>\n<ol>\n<li><strong>Location</strong> – Panama City is huge, and it can take some time to get around. Pick a place that is central to the sites you want to see and nightlife you want to enjoy. (All the hostels listed here are in central locations.)</li>\n<li><strong>Price</strong> – In Panama City, you really get what you pay for, so if you go with a really cheap place, you&#8217;re probably going to get a hostel that is small and cramped and doesn&#8217;t offer great service.</li>\n<li><strong>Amenities</strong> – Every hostel in town offers free Wi-Fi, and most have a free breakfast, but if you want more than that, be sure to do your research to find the one that best meets your needs!</li>\n<li><strong>Staff</strong> &#8211; All the hostels listed here have amazing staff who are super friendly and knowledgeable. Even if you don&#8217;t end up staying at one of the places listed below, be sure to look up reviews to ensure that you end up somewhere where the staff is helpful and friendly. They can make or break a hostel!</li>\n</ol>\n<p>To help you plan your trip, here is my list of the hostels in Panama City that I like the most. If you don’t want to read the longer list below, the following hostels are the best in each category:</p>\n<p><strong>Best Hostel for Budget Travelers</strong>: <a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fpwa%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FHostal-Casa-Areka%2FPanama-City%2F43562\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">Hostal Casa Areka</a><br />\n<strong>Best Hostel for Families</strong>: <a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fpwa%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FMagnolia-Inn-Casco-Viejo%2FPanama-City%2F59863\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">Magnolia Inn Casa Viejo</a><br />\n<strong>Best Hostel for Solo Female Travelers</strong>: <a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fpwa%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FEl-Machico-Hostel%2FPanama-City%2F88333\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">El Machio</a><br />\n<strong>Best Hostel for Digital Nomads</strong>: <a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fpwa%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FSelina-Casco-Viejo-Panama-City%2FPanama-City%2F285048\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">Selina Casco Viejo</a><br />\n<strong>Best Hostel for Partying</strong>: <a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fpwa%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FHostal-Casa-Areka%2FPanama-City%2F43562\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">Hostal Casa Areka</a><br />\n<strong>Best Overall Hostel</strong>: <a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fpwa%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FLuna-s-Castle-Hostel%2FPanama-City%2F39099\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">Luna&#8217;s Castle Hostel</a></p>\n<p>Want more specifics for each hostel? Here&#8217;s my comprehensive list of the best hostels in Panama City:</p>\n<p><strong>Price Legend (per night)</strong></p>\n<ul>\n<li>$ = Under $15 USD</li>\n<li>$$ = $15-20 USD</li>\n<li>$$$ = Over $20 USD</li>\n</ul>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<h3>1. Magnolia Inn Casco Viejo</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/panamahostel1.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The posh interior of the Magnolia Inn Casa Viejo hostel in Panama City\"><br />\nThis boutique hostel is located in Casco Viejo, the city&#8217;s beautiful Old Town. It&#8217;s clean and quiet, making it a good choice for families or travelers looking for some downtime. The hostel is an old French colonial mansion and balances historic charm with modern amenities (like AC, Wi-Fi, and hot showers). The beds are basic and don&#8217;t have curtains, but the mattresses are thick and comfy. There are also a few common areas where you can relax and hang out or watch TV. Since it&#8217;s quiet, I&#8217;d suggest staying here if you want to get a good night&#8217;s sleep. There are several social hostels nearby where you can grab a drink and hang out, so you can enjoy being social before returning to your quiet hostel. </p>\n<p><strong>Magnolia Inn Casco Viejo at a glance</strong>:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>$$</li>\n<li>Central location in the Old Town</li>\n<li>Clean and quiet</li>\n<li>Beautiful interior</li>\n</ul>\n<p><em>Beds from $16 USD a night, rooms from $116 USD.</em></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fpwa%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FMagnolia-Inn-Casco-Viejo%2FPanama-City%2F59863\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">—> Book your stay at Magnolia Inn Casco Viejo!</a><br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>2. Hostal Casa Areka</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/panamahostel2.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The outdoor swimming pool and hang out area at Hostal Casa Areka in Panama City\"><br />\nThis energetic hostel has a pool, outdoor Wi-Fi, space to barbecue, and a spacious kitchen for cooking your own meals. It&#8217;s also surrounded by bars and restaurants, making it a good choice for those who want to party. There are lots of common areas to relax in. The beds are pretty basic (no curtains for privacy) but are comfortable enough. The dorms also only have eight beds (or fewer), so you&#8217;re never crammed in with other people, and there are female-only dorms too. Only some of the showers have hot water, however, but it is the cheapest hostel in town.</p>\n<p><strong>Hostal Casa Areka at a glance</strong>:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>$</li>\n<li>Swimming pool</li>\n<li>Super affordable</li>\n<li>Free breakfast</li>\n</ul>\n<p><em>Beds from $9 USD a night, rooms from $35 USD.</em></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fpwa%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FHostal-Casa-Areka%2FPanama-City%2F43562\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">—> Book your stay at Hostal Casa Areka!</a><br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>3. El Machio</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/panamahostel3.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The colorful dorm rooms of El Machio Hostel in Panama City\"><br />\nThis is a social hostel where it&#8217;s really easy to meet people, since they have a pool and a small bar, play movies outside, and organize tons of tours (including affordable trips to the <a href=\"https://www.nomadicmatt.com/travel-blogs/top-ten-best-tropical-islands/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">San Blas Islands</a>). The beds aren&#8217;t the best, but the dorms have lockers to keep your items safe and there&#8217;s hot water in the showers. They also have female-only dorms. Breakfast is included, there&#8217;s a spacious kitchen for cooking, and the surrounding neighborhood is quite safe too. </p>\n<p><strong>El Machio at a glance</strong>:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>$</li>\n<li>Social atmosphere makes it easy to meet people</li>\n<li>Free brekafast</li>\n<li>Female-only dorms for added privacy and security</li>\n</ul>\n<p><em>Beds from $13 USD a night, rooms from $50 USD.</em></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fpwa%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FEl-Machico-Hostel%2FPanama-City%2F88333\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">—> Book your stay at El Machio!</a><br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>4. Luna&#8217;s Castle Hostel</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/panamahostel4.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The cool interior design of Luna's Castle Hostel in Panama City\"><br />\nThis is my favorite hostel in Panama City. Housed in an old colonial mansion overlooking the ocean, it&#8217;s a cool backpacker hostel with a laid-back vibe. Free breakfast is included, there&#8217;s a bar on-site for having fun, the showers have hot water, and the staff go above and beyond: they organize walking tours and other fun activities to ensure that you have an amazing visit and meet cool people during your stay. There are only large dorms (10 or 12 beds), but the beds have curtains and the mattresses are comfy. It&#8217;s lively, social, and an institution on the Gringo Trail through Central America.</p>\n<p><strong>Luna&#8217;s Castle Hostel at a glance</strong>:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>$$</li>\n<li>Free breakfast</li>\n<li>Easy to meet people</li>\n<li>Beautiful location by the ocean</li>\n</ul>\n<p><em>Beds from $16 USD a night.</em></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fpwa%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FLuna-s-Castle-Hostel%2FPanama-City%2F39099\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">—> Book your stay at Luna&#8217;s Castle Hostel!</a><br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>5. Zebulo Hostel</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/panamahostel5.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The spacious and empty dorm rooms of Zebulo Hostel in Panama City\"><br />\nZebulo has lots of free perks, including free breakfast, free coffee and tea, and a jacuzzi on-site. While the dorm beds are basic (squeaky metal bunks with no curtains), they&#8217;re comfortable enough and not crowded (capped at nine beds). It also has the cheapest private rooms in the city; however, there&#8217;s no hot water. The staff also organize tons of tours, such as trips to <a href=\"https://www.nomadicmatt.com/travel-guides/colombia-travel-tips/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Colombia</a> and the San Blas Islands. They also host lots of weekly events (like BBQ nights). It&#8217;s a laid-back hostel that makes it easy to meet people and enjoy all the city has to offer. </p>\n<p><strong>Zebulo Hostel at a glance</strong>:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>$</li>\n<li>Affordable private rooms</li>\n<li>Lots of free perks</li>\n<li>Tons of tours and activities</li>\n</ul>\n<p><em>Beds from $10 USD a night, rooms from $22 USD.</em></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fpwa%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FZebulo-Hostel%2FPanama-City%2F273588\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">—> Book your stay at Zebulo Hostel!</a><br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>6. Selina Casco Viejo</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/panamahostel6.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"A classy and spacious dorm room in Selina Casco Viejo hostel in Panama City\"><br />\nLocated in the picturesque Old Town (in yet another historic colonial building), Selina is new hostel. It&#8217;s a chic, upscale spot that&#8217;s popular with solo travelers and digital nomads. There&#8217;s a spacious outdoor patio for hanging out and lots of bars nearby. The beds are comfy, and the showers have hot water (which is a nice perk, since many cheaper hostels in the city don&#8217;t have hot water). There&#8217;s AC to keep you cool, a co-working space, a pool table, and lots of common areas for chilling out. </p>\n<p><strong>Selina Casco Viejo at a glance</strong>:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>$</li>\n<li>Lots of common areas to hangout in</li>\n<li>Social atmosphere</li>\n<li>Central location in the Old Town</li>\n</ul>\n<p><em>Beds from $14 USD a night, $36 USD.</em></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fpwa%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FSelina-Casco-Viejo-Panama-City%2FPanama-City%2F285048\" rel=\"noopener nofollow noreferrer\">—> Book your stay at Selina Casco Viejo!</a></p>\n<p><center>***</center></p>\n<p>Whether you&#8217;re looking to party or just want to relax and enjoy your trip alone, you&#8217;ll be able to find an affordable hostel in <a href=\"https://www.nomadicmatt.com/travel-guides/panama-travel-tips/panama-city/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Panama City</a> that won&#8217;t disappoint you!</p>\n<div class=\"single-booking\">\n<h4>Book Your Trip to Panama: Logistical Tips and Tricks</h4>\n<p><strong>Book Your Flight</strong><br />\nFind a cheap flight by using <a href=\"http://www.anrdoezrs.net/click-3032045-12837948\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Skyscanner</a> or <a href=\"https://www.momondo.com/\">Momondo</a>. src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/alberta1a.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The peaceful scenery of Banff, Alberta\"><br />\n<strong>Posted</strong>: 7/6/20 | July 6th, 2020</p>\n<p><em>Dalene and Pete Heck, the duo behind Hecktic Travels is also the team at <a href=\"https://www.roadtripalberta.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Road Trip Alberta</a>! Dalene and Pete are Alberta raised and currently living in the province’s third-biggest city, Lethbridge. Alberta is one of the most scenic provinces in Canada and, today, Dalene shares a driving itinerary hitting many of her favorite Alberta sights.</em></p>\n<p>Arguably Canada’s most beautiful province, Alberta is known primarily for the mountain hub of Banff National Park. Millions descend annually on Calgary airport and then high-tail it west for an hour and a half to visit this gem of the Rockies. The draw of Banff is entirely warranted but many of these visitors often miss out on everything else that Alberta has to offer.</p>\n<p>Its cities are dynamic, other mountain towns are just as gorgeous and with fewer tourists, the southeastern side of the province is home to a trove of dinosaur bones, and the north is covered in lush forests and teeming with wildlife and outdoor adventures eager to be had.</p>\n<p>As a born-and-raised Albertan, I left in my early thirties to see more of the world, craving exploration. When I returned almost a decade later, I did so with fresh eyes and an appreciation for the land that shaped me. </p>\n<p>This article outlines a ten-day road trip itinerary shares some of my favorite spots in the province that will help you see more than crowds of tourists in Banff!<br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>Day 1: Calgary</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/alberta1.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The towering skyline of Calgary, Alberta, Canada in the autumn\"></p>\n<p>Dubbed “Cowtown” due to its roots in the cattle industry, <a href=\"https://www.nomadicmatt.com/travel-guides/canada-travel-tips/calgary/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Calgary</a> is Alberta’s largest city (1.37 million people). Balancing modern urban architecture with friendly, small-town vibes, Calgary is a curious melting pot of folks from many backgrounds. It’s also home to an array of activities and a trendy food scene that will ensure that your days and tummies are full.</p>\n<p><strong>Start Downtown</strong><br />\nExplore the Bow River’s network of walking and biking trails. See the prime photo spot of the Peace Bridge. For another prime photo op and to gaze upon an architectural wonder, don’t miss the Calgary Public Library, which was named one of the 100 Greatest Places of 2019 by Time magazine.</p>\n<p>Not far from the library is Prince’s Island Park, which is a hub for cultural events. It’s home to the Calgary Folk Music Festival (in late July) and the esteemed River Café (a pricey restaurant but well worth it), and near to Eau Claire Market, which has some mouth-watering eats and specialty merchandise.</p>\n<p><strong>Fuel Up on Good Eats</strong><br />\nDon’t miss out on Tubby Dog for a cheap, delicious, and fun meal? Play some classic arcade games while you try the Sumo (a dog with pickled ginger, Japanese mayo, wasabi, and seaweed salad) or the A-bomb (a dog with all the classic trimmings, plus a healthy dump of potato chips right on top). Another one of my faves is Native Tongues, which offers upscale Mexican food in the city center. </p>\n<p><strong>Consider Planning Your Visit Around These Festivals</strong><br />\nThe Calgary Stampede — also known as “the greatest outdoor show on earth” — takes over the city for ten days in early July. The world-class rodeo is just one facet of the event. There’s also a spectacular grandstand show plus all the rides and deep-fried festival foods you would expect. It’s also a giant, messy party too.</p>\n<p>Beakerhead, held annually in mid-September, brings together the worlds of art, science, and engineering. Imagine a massive party filled with fire-shooting robots, an interactive science lesson on how to make the best chocolate chip cookie, and playing a giant life-sized version of Snakes &#038; Ladders. It’s the best nerd party of the year. </p>\n<p><strong>Where to stay in Calgary</strong></p>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.booking.com/hotel/ca/howard-johnson-express-inn-calgary.en.html?aid=1383362&#038;no_rooms=1&#038;group_adults=2\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Canada’s Best Value Inn Chinook Station</a> &#8211; Located near the Chinook LRT Station, this hotel features a continental breakfast, with rooms available starting as low as $49 CAD/night.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FHI-Calgary-City-Centre%2FCalgary%2F2138\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">HI Calgary City Centre</a> &#8211; If you happen to be a member of HI Canada, consider this hostel, located in the downtown core, just a two-minute walk to the C-train (local transit) station.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.booking.com/hotel/ca/arts-calgary.en.html?aid=1383362&#038;no_rooms=1&#038;group_adults=2\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Hotel Arts</a> &#8211; For more upscale and eclectic lodging near downtown, this hotel has top-rated amenities for a reasonable price.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<h3>Day 2: Banff</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/alberta2.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The picturesque city of Banff, Alberta, Canada with mountains in the distance\"><br />\nNext, head from <a href=\"https://roadtripalberta.com/calgary-to-banff/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Calgary to Banff</a>, which takes about an hour and a half by car.</p>\n<p>Note: You’ll need to purchase a park pass upon arrival at the gates just outside of town, or you can <a href=\"https://www.banfflakelouise.com/park-pass-purchase\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">buy one online</a>. The current daily rate for an adult is $10.00 CAD, and it will expire at 4:00 pm the following day.</p>\n<p>If you’re planning on visiting multiple parks, you might consider a Parks Canada “Discovery Pass” for $69.19 CAD, which can be used for multiple days and will grant you entry to all Canadian national parks for one full year.</p>\n<p>There are too many amazing hikes to list, but start with the iconic Johnston Canyon. Keep it short with a 30-minute walk to the Lower Falls, or plan for a full four-hour trek all the way to the Ink Pots. (For more info, read this <a href=\"https://roadtripalberta.com/best-hikes-in-banff/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">guide to hiking in Banff</a>.)</p>\n<p>To really get the adrenaline pumping, head to Mt. Norquay for the Via Ferrata hike. Cross suspension bridges and climb ladders on the edge of a mountain, all while safely harnessed and led by an experienced guide.</p>\n<p>There are also plenty of options for canoeing, kayaking, and stand-up paddleboarding on a number of nearby lakes. Visit the Banff Canoe Club in town for rentals.</p>\n<p>Winter is a prime time to visit if you’re a ski bunny. Three mountains in the area known collectively as Ski Big 3 (Banff Sunshine, the Lake Louise Ski Resort, and Mt. Norquay) are all world-class.</p>\n<p>Be sure to take the Banff Gondola up Sulphur Mountain for some epic views. It’s open year-round, and it has an impressive interpretive center and scenic boardwalk at the top, and even two restaurants.</p>\n<p>Nearby is also the stunning Banff Upper Hot Springs.</p>\n<p><strong>Where to Eat</strong><br />\nWild Flour Bakery, known for its nourishing baked goods and good coffee, is an excellent stop to fill your tank at any time of day.</p>\n<p>Eager to try some Canadian wild meats? Head to the Grizzly House to cook up your own bison, elk, or a number of other options using a hot stone at your table. The decor is severely outdated, but the experience is a must-do. Not a meat-eater? Head to Nourish Bistro for the best plant-based food in Banff.</p>\n<p><strong>Where to Stay in Banff</strong></p>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FBanff-International-Hostel%2FBanff%2F66387\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Banff International Hostel</a> &#8211; Just a few blocks from the heart of downtown, this hostel is a comfortable place to rest your head after a long day of exploring!</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.booking.com/hotel/ca/banff-y-mountain-lodge.en.html?aid=1383362&#038;no_rooms=1&#038;group_adults=2\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">YWCA Banff Hotel</a> &#8211; The perfect hideaway in the mountains for those looking for a comfortable and budget-friendly accommodation.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FHI-Banff-Alpine-Centre%2FBanff%2F1569\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">HI Banff Alpine Centre</a> &#8211; If you’re a member of the HI community, you may want to stay at this location, the largest hostel in Alberta.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<h3>Day 3: Banff and Lake Louise</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/alberta3.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"Lake Louise and Banff at night under a starry sky\"><br />\nIf you’re an early riser, head 15 minutes north to Two Jack Lake to catch a gorgeous sunrise. If it’s a clearer morning, bright red, orange, and purple will stain the sky and lake, silhouetting the mountain and creating a truly epic sight.</p>\n<p>If there was anything left on your to-do list from the day before, finish that up now, but plan for almost a whole day around Lake Louise.</p>\n<p><strong>While in Lake Louise&#8230;.</strong><br />\nThe Fairmont Chateau Lake Louise is the major draw in the area, and walking its halls is a must before you venture on any number of outdoor activities.</p>\n<p>If you are there in summer, consider the Lake Agnes Tea House hike for its views and the unique experience of taking tea on top of the world (remember to bring cash, as they don’t have other payment options on-site). It is a short 2.2mile (3.5 km) hike, but you can also continue on to Lake Agnes itself. </p>\n<p>Feeling adventurous? Then take “the Tea House Challenge” and visit the other one, too, The Plain of Six Glaciers Tea House, for a 9 mile (14.5 km) total hike on the Highline Trail.</p>\n<p>If you are there in winter, skating, snowshoeing, dog-sledding, sleigh rides, and more are all available from the hotel. You will have no problem filling your day in one of the most beautiful spots in all of Canada.</p>\n<p>Dining options are fewer in the very small town of Lake Louise, but find the Trailhead Café for a budget-friendly and supremely delicious meal. There are also several options inside the Chateau itself, but I recommend Alpine Social for its laid-back atmosphere and hearty food.<br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>Day 4: Driving from Banff to Jasper</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/alberta4.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The beautiful landscape of Alberta, Canada between Banff and Jasper\"><br />\nDrive from Banff to Jasper via the Icefields Parkway. The drive itself is about 3.5 hours, but I suggest that you plan for a whole day as there are lots of stops to make along the way. </p>\n<p>The Icefields Parkway is breathtaking. Take it slow and stop often to really absorb the beauty of this day. (Do, however, consult the weather forecast and <a href=\"https://511.alberta.ca/#:Alerts\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">road conditions</a>, as it can often be closed in winter.)</p>\n<p><strong>Making the Drive</strong><br />\nFill up the car with gas and pack a picnic lunch before leaving Banff, as there is only one place to stop for snacks en route (Saskatchewan River Crossing) but it is closed in winter. But once you are safely on your way, here are just a few of the stops you can make:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Leave early to catch sunrise over Vermillion Lakes, just outside of Banff as you begin your journey north.</li>\n<li>Peyto Lake is a must-see. You have undoubtedly seen its image before; now it’s time to see it for yourself! From your car it’s just a short walk up a hill to get to the viewpoint and take in that stark aquamarine water from above.</li>\n<li>The Columbia Icefield, just an hour before Jasper, is the largest in the Canadian Rockies. You can take a tour to walk right on the glacier and/or take a stroll on the glass-floored Icefield Skywalk lookout to see everything from above.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>There is much more to see! This <a href=\"https://roadtripalberta.com/banff-to-jasper/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Banff-to-Jasper article</a> maps it all out for you.</p>\n<p><strong>Where to Stay in Jasper</strong></p>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FJasper-Downtown-Hostel%2FJasper%2F263493\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Jasper Downtown Hostel</a> &#8211; Conveniently situated in the heart of downtown Jasper, this modern hostel won’t break the bank; its private rooms start as low as $63 CAD/night.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FHI-Jasper%2FJasper%2F295773\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">HI Jasper</a> &#8211; Just a short walk to downtown, the HI Hostel Jasper was opened in June 2019. Choose between private rooms, shared rooms for four, and family rooms.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.booking.com/hotel/ca/maligne-lodge.en.html?aid=1383362&#038;no_rooms=1&#038;group_adults=2\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Maligne Lodge</a> &#8211; Conveniently tucked at the edge of Jasper’s main street, where the mountains end and the town begins, this is a great budget-friendly hotel. </li>\n</ul>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<h3>Days 5 &#038; 6: Jasper</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/alberta5.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The huge elk standing near a small lake in Alberta, Canada near Jasper\"><br />\nJasper is the largest park in the Canadian Rockies and one of fifteen UNESCO World Heritage Sites in the country. Rougher around the edges than its southern brother Banff, it’s the spot to hit if you’re craving fewer crowds and small-town charm. </p>\n<p>Spirit Island is one of the most photographed spots in Canada. You can canoe out there and reach this spot on Maligne Lake in half a day. If you don&#8217;t feel like doing that, boat cruises are available too! </p>\n<p>Moreover, take advantage of your remote location and book a tour to see some iconic Canadian wildlife (bears, elk, mountain goats, moose, and more). While such encounters may occur by chance on your visit, a guided tour will increase your chances and is a great way to gain local knowledge.</p>\n<p>Additionally, in October, the Jasper Dark Sky Festival takes place.The park has ideal conditions for this given that there is so little light pollution. If you can’t make it there, the Jasper Planetarium is open year-round for star viewing.</p>\n<p>There are so many hiking options. Start with a short jaunt to Athabasca Falls (less than an hour round-trip), and then ramp up according to your fitness level. (See this article about <a href=\"https://roadtripalberta.com/what-to-do-in-jasper/#Hiking\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\">best Jasper hikes</a> to decide what comes next.)</p>\n<p>Just north of town is Maligne Canyon, and in winter, you can walk on and explore the frozen river (be sure you have ice cleats on). In the summer, you can hike in the canyon, and the winding trail has six suspension bridges spanning the gorge.</p>\n<p>Take a load off and ride up the Jasper Skytram to experience the best mountain views. On a clear day, you can even see peaks in neighboring British Columbia. Enjoy the seven-minute ride up and have a bite at the Summit Restaurant at the top. </p>\n<p><strong>Must-Eats</strong><br />\nStop at the Bright Spot Family Restaurant for the big country breakfast, which will stick to your bones and give you energy for your day. Whistle Stop Pub is also good for a pint and snack. Canada’s very first national park brewery, Jasper Brewing Company, is also here. Along with six signature brews that are made on-site, the large restaurant offers elevated pub fare.<br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>Day 7: Driving from Jasper to Edmonton</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/alberta6.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The stunning vista between Jasper and Edmonton in Alberta, Canada\"><br />\nThe four-hour drive from <a href=\"https://roadtripalberta.com/edmonton-to-jasper/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Jasper to Edmonton</a> is not the most exciting (the scenic views drop off quickly outside of the national park), but there are a couple of stops you can make along the way to spice it up.</p>\n<p>If you don’t hit up Miette Hot Springs during your stay in Jasper, then it’s an easy stop on the way out of town. It is home to the hottest spring water in the Canadian Rockies! It requires a little detour off of the main highway, but the drive through the Fiddle Valley alone makes it worth the trip.</p>\n<p>An hour into your journey, you can make a stop in Hinton to see the most iconic of local wildlife: the humble beaver. Stretch your legs along the nearly 2 mile (3 km) Beaver Boardwalk, and hopefully, you’ll spot Canada’s national animal. </p>\n<p>This is also a great place to plan to have lunch: The Old Grind has an extensive menu that includes vegetarian and vegan options.</p>\n<p><strong>Arriving in Edmonton</strong><br />\nDepending on what time you left Jasper, the driving conditions you encountered (add more time in winter!), and how many stops you made along the way, you may arrive with extra time to explore Alberta’s capital city. And my guess is that those car-bound legs are going to need a stretch.</p>\n<p>As you drive into the west side of Edmonton, this would be the perfect occasion to take a long walk in the largest mall in North America. West Edmonton Mall is home to over 800 stories and services, and it contains theme parks, multiple movie theaters, a ridiculously fun indoor water park, and even a large skating rink. </p>\n<p>Enjoying the mall can easily take up the rest of your day (and the next one, if you are a shopper).<br />\n&#160;</p>\n<h3>Days 8 &#038; 9: Edmonton</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/alberta7.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"The skyline of Edmonton, Alberta, Canada during autumn\"><br />\nTeeming with history and culture rich as hot chocolate, Alberta’s capital city is the perfect way to finish off your tour of the province. Edmonton has been dubbed “the festival city” on account of its year-round cultural festivals, so you’ll never be short on things to do here. </p>\n<p>The Fringe Festival is the biggest and oldest of its kind in North America and offers a dynamic theater experience. Running annually for ten days in the middle of August, it often attracts more than 1,500 local, national, and international artists, who give well over a thousand performances across the city.</p>\n<p>The Silver Skate Festival is becoming one of the premier events in Alberta to celebrate and embrace winter. One highlight is the opening of the ice castles in Hawrelak Park, typically several weeks before the February festival. During the ten days of the festival itself, expect snow sculpting, skate races, helicopter tours, and more.</p>\n<p>If you aren’t in Edmonton during a festival, take time and stroll through the grounds of the Alberta Legislature. Not only is “the Ledge” an architectural journey into the past (construction was started in 1907) but you can also learn about the Canadian government, Alberta’s political history, and the art and architecture of the building by taking a free tour. </p>\n<p>Edmonton’s river valley is the largest urban park in North America, with 100 miles (160 kms) of maintained paths. So you don’t even have to leave the city itself to explore nature! Walk and cycle as far as you like, taking in any (or all) of the 20 city parks along the river. </p>\n<p>Head for the Neon Sign Museum one night. This collection of 20 functional historic signs tells the story of Edmonton’s neon past al fresco. This exhibit is completely free and open 24/7.</p>\n<p>If you didn’t get your wildlife fill in the Rockies, then head a short distance outside of the city to Elk Island National Park. Elk Island is the only fenced national park in Canada, a conservation effort to help bring the bison population back. </p>\n<p>And you didn’t think I’d go this entire post without mentioning a hockey game, did you? The Edmonton Oilers play in one of the newest arenas in the NHL, so catch a game if you can, especially if they are playing their provincial rivals, the Calgary Flames. </p>\n<p>If you are visiting in summer, you can also watch a heated Canadian football (not soccer) battle between the Edmonton Eskimos and the Calgary Stampeders.</p>\n<p><strong>Can’t-Miss Food and Drink</strong><br />\nStop at Duchess Bake Shop. This Parisian-inspired café blends some of Alberta’s favorite flavors with French pastries, all made from scratch daily. It’s regularly mentioned as one of the best cafés in the city.</p>\n<p>Hathaway’s Diner has quality food at reasonable prices. And who doesn’t love old-school-diner kitsch?</p>\n<p>A few years ago, Alberta’s tax system changed up the way it categorized breweries, which resulted in an explosion of craft beer across the province. Don’t miss a stop at Craft Beer Market as it offers up Canada’s largest selection of craft brews. </p>\n<p><strong>Where to Stay in Edmonton</strong></p>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj/destination:https%3A%2F%2Fwww.hostelworld.com%2Fhosteldetails.php%2FHI-Edmonton%2FEdmonton%2F4651\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">HI Edmonton</a> &#8211; Located just off of Whyte Avenue in Edmonton’s historic Old Strathcona neighborhood, this hostel is right near the river valley park system (also many bus stops to get to other destinations).</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.booking.com/hotel/ca/days-inn-downtown-edm.en.html?aid=1383362&#038;no_rooms=1&#038;group_adults=2\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Days Inn Downtown</a> &#8211; Conveniently located in the downtown core and only minutes away from local attractions, this hotel is an excellent option for those not wanting to give up comfort while staying on budget.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<h3>Day 10: Driving to Calgary</h3>\n<p><img src=\"https://media.nomadicmatt.com/2020/alberta8.jpg\" width=\"675\" height=\"395\" alt=\"One of the funny displays in the Gopher Hole Museum in Alberta, Canada\"><br />\nIt only takes three hours to drive from Edmonton to Calgary on a busy highway. Use your last day to visit more of Calgary. </p>\n<p>If you have time, visit the Heritage Ranch near Red Deer (about halfway through the drive). A rancher will drop you off in the middle of the wilderness with a map and a compass (or a GPS). Your goal is to remain at large and capture four designated flags within an hour. All the while, you are being hunted by a man on a horse. It is terrifying and exhilarating and everything in between!</p>\n<p>A little closer to <a href=\"https://www.nomadicmatt.com/travel-guides/canada-travel-tips/calgary/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Calgary</a>, you can turn off the main highway into Torrington and find the Gopher Hole Museum. Gopher overpopulation is a problem in the area, and so the residents wanted to create something quirky to bring in tourists. The museum is one small room of taxidermied rodents staged in a variety of scenes that highlight local life (think curling gophers, beautician gophers, etc.). It will take no more than a half-hour to visit, but it is well worth the detour for all the WTF moments to be had. </p>\n<p><center>***</center></p>\n<p>Alberta is a very big province. By comparison, Texas is only 2% bigger. If it is the mountains that call you here, then that is rightly so, but I hope you will also take the time to explore other parts of this land rich in attractions. They will keep anyone and everyone entertained for ten days and beyond!</p>\n<p><em>Dalene Heck and her husband Pete are behind the blog <a href=\"http://www.hecktictravels.com/\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\" target=\"_blank\">Hecktic Travels</a>, which chronicles their journey since selling all their belongings in 2009. They’ve recently started the website <a href=\"https://www.roadtripalberta.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Road Trip Alberta</a> to encourage people to visit their home provence.</em></p>\n<div class=\"single-booking\">\n<h4>Book Your Trip to Canada: Logistical Tips and Tricks</h4>\n<p><strong>Book Your Flight</strong><br />\nFind a cheap flight by using <a href=\"http://www.anrdoezrs.net/click-3032045-12837948\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Skyscanner</a> or <a href=\"https://www.momondo.com/\">Momondo</a>. They are my two favorite search engines because they search websites and airlines around the globe so you always know no stone is left unturned.</p>\n<p><strong>Book Your Accommodation</strong><br />\nYou can book your hostel with <a href=\"https://prf.hn/click/camref:1101lHtj\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Hostelworld</a>. If you want to stay elsewhere, use <a href=\"https://www.booking.com/index.html?aid=362916\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Booking.com</a> as they consistently return the cheapest rates for guesthouses and cheap hotels. </p>\n<p><strong>Don&#8217;t Forget Travel Insurance</strong><br />\nTravel insurance will protect you against illness, injury, theft, and cancellations. It&#8217;s comprehensive protection in case anything goes wrong. I never go on a trip without it as I&#8217;ve had to use it many times in the past. I&#8217;ve been using <a href=\"https://www.worldnomads.com/lovedby/nomadic-matt?affiliate=nmts&#38;subId=brandlink&#38;affiliateTrackingId=0fe898ceef264503a88f74f4bbc7bb5b&#38;utm_source=nmts&#38;utm_medium=affiliate&#38;utm_campaign=Affiliate&#38;utm_content=brandlink\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">World Nomads</a> for ten years.
